Stockholder: </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You are cordially invited to attend the 2020 Annual Meeting of Stockholders (the &#147;Meeting&#148;) of Goldman Sachs BDC,
Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) to be held on June&nbsp;17, 2020, at 10:00 a.m. (Eastern time). The Meeting will be conducted as a virtual meeting hosted by means of a live webcast. The Board of Directors of the Company has implemented a virtual
meeting format this year primarily to reflect our and global concerns regarding the spread of <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">COVID-19.</FONT> Stockholders will be able to listen, vote, and submit questions from their home or any location with
internet connectivity. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You or your proxyholder will be able to attend the Meeting online, vote and submit questions by visiting
www.meetingcenter.io/243329110 and using a control number assigned by Computershare Fund Services. To register and receive access to the virtual meeting, you will need to follow the instructions provided in the Notice of Annual Meeting and Proxy
Statement that follow. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>The Meeting is being held (i)&nbsp;to elect two Class&nbsp;III directors of the Company, who will each serve
until the 2023 annual meeting of stockholders or until his or her successor is duly elected and qualified, and (ii)&nbsp;to ratify the selection of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP as the Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm for
the fiscal year ending December&nbsp;31, 2020. </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">A formal Notice of Annual Meeting and Proxy Statement setting forth in detail the
matters to come before the Meeting are attached hereto, and a proxy card is enclosed for your use. You should read the Proxy Statement carefully. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>WHETHER OR NOT YOU PLAN TO BE PRESENT AT THE MEETING, YOUR VOTE IS VERY IMPORTANT. </B>If you do not plan to be present at the virtual
Meeting, you can vote by signing, dating and returning the enclosed proxy card promptly or by using the Internet or telephone voting options as described on your proxy card. If you have any questions regarding the proxy materials, please contact the
Company at <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(888)&nbsp;916-1722.</FONT> Your prompt response will help reduce proxy costs&#151;which are paid by the Company and indirectly by its stockholders&#151;and will also mean that you can avoid receiving <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">follow-up</FONT> phone calls and mailings. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:55%; text-indent:-2%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Sincerely, </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:55%; text-indent:-2%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">/s/ Brendan McGovern </P>

the Proxy Statement attached to this Notice. On May&nbsp;4, 2020, the Board of Directors of the Company, including each of the independent directors, unanimously recommended that you vote <B>&#147;FOR&#148; </B>each of the Proposals. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You will be able to attend the Meeting online, submit your questions during the meeting and vote your shares electronically at the meeting by
going to www.meetingcenter.io/243329110 and entering your control number, which is included on the proxy card that you received. The password to attend the meeting is BDC2020. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">If your shares are held through a stock brokerage account or by a bank or other holder of record you will need to request a legal proxy in
order to receive access to the virtual meeting. To do so, you must submit proof of your proxy power (legal proxy) reflecting your holdings along with your name and email address to Computershare Fund Services. Requests for registration must be
labeled as &#147;Legal Proxy&#148; and be received no later than 5:00 p.m., Eastern Time, on June&nbsp;15, 2020. You will receive a confirmation of your registration by email that includes the control number necessary to access and vote at the
meeting. Requests for registration should be directed to Computershare at shareholdermeetings@computershare.com. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The meeting webcast will
begin promptly at 10:00 a.m. (Eastern time). We encourage you to access the meeting prior to the start time. For additional information on how you can attend and participate in the virtual Meeting, please see the instructions beginning on page 6 of
the proxy statement that follows. Because the Meeting will be a completely virtual meeting, there will be no physical location for stockholders to attend. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Stockholders of record at the close of business on May&nbsp;11, 2020 are entitled to receive notice of, and to vote at, the Meeting and at any
postponements or adjournments thereof. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Your vote is extremely important to us. If you will not attend the virtual Meeting, we urge you to
sign, date and promptly return the enclosed proxy card in the envelope provided, which is addressed for your convenience and needs no postage if mailed in the United States. You may also vote easily and quickly by Internet or by telephone. In the
event there are not sufficient votes for a quorum or to approve the Proposals at the time of the </P>

envelope provided (unless you are voting by Internet or by telephone). <B>If you sign, date and return a proxy card but give no voting instructions, your shares will be voted &#147;FOR&#148; all of the proposals indicated on the card. </B>If you

instructions. Stockholders outside the United States should vote via the Internet or by submitting a proxy card instead. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">You may revoke

<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>OF </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>GOLDMAN SACHS BDC,

<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="right">May&nbsp;12, 2020 </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This Proxy
Statement is furnished in connection with the solicitation of proxies by and on behalf of the Board of Directors (the &#147;Board&#148;) of Goldman Sachs BDC, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) for use at the 2020 Annual Meeting of Stockholders (the
&#147;Meeting&#148;), to be held virtually on June&nbsp;17, 2020, at 10:00 a.m. (Eastern time), and any postponement or adjournment thereof. Much of the information in this Proxy Statement is required under rules of the Securities and Exchange
Commission (the &#147;SEC&#148;), and some of it is technical in nature. If there is anything you do not understand, please contact the Company at (888) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">916-1722.</FONT> </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">This Proxy Statement, the accompanying Notice of Annual Meeting and proxy card and the Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> for the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 are being mailed to stockholders (the &#147;Stockholders&#148;) of the Company of record as of May, 11, 2020 (the &#147;Record Date&#148;) on or about May&nbsp;27,
2020. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>PURPOSE OF THE MEETING </B></P>

stockholders or until his or her successor is duly elected and qualified (&#147;Proposal 1&#148;); and </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

accounting firm for the fiscal year ending December&nbsp;31, 2020 (&#147;Proposal 2&#148;). </P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>INFORMATION REGARDING
ATTENDING THE MEETING </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Meeting will be a virtual meeting conducted exclusively via live webcast starting at 10:00 a.m. (Eastern
time). You will be able to attend the Meeting online, submit your questions during the meeting and vote your shares electronically at the meeting by going to www.meetingcenter.io/243329110 and entering your control number, which is included on the
proxy card that you received. The password to attend the meeting is BDC2020. Because the Meeting is completely virtual and being conducted via live webcast, stockholders will not be able to attend the meeting in person. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">If your shares are held through a stock brokerage account or by a bank or other holder of record you will need to request a legal proxy in
order to receive access to the virtual meeting. To do so, you must submit proof of your proxy power (legal proxy) reflecting your holdings along with your name and email address to Computershare Fund Services. Requests for registration must be
labeled as &#147;Legal Proxy&#148; and be received no </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">1 </P>

later than 5:00 p.m., Eastern Time, on June&nbsp;15, 2020. You will receive a confirmation of your registration by email that includes the control number necessary to access and vote at the
meeting. Requests for registration should be directed to Computershare at shareholdermeetings@computershare.com. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">In light of the rapidly
changing developments related to coronavirus <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">(COVID-19),</FONT> we are pleased to offer our stockholders a completely virtual Meeting, which provides worldwide access and communication, while protecting the health
and safety of our stockholders, directors, management and other stakeholders. We are committed to ensuring that stockholders will be afforded the same rights and opportunities to participate as they would at an
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">in-person</FONT> meeting. We will try to answer as many stockholder-submitted questions as time permits that comply with the Meeting rules of conduct. However, we reserve the right to edit profanity or other
inappropriate language, or to exclude questions that are not pertinent to meeting matters or that are otherwise inappropriate. If substantially similar questions are received, we will group such questions together and provide a single response to
avoid repetition. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>INFORMATION REGARDING THIS SOLICITATION </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">It is expected that the solicitation of proxies will be primarily by mail. The Company&#146;s officers, and personnel of the Company&#146;s
investment adviser, GSAM, and the Company&#146;s transfer agent and any authorized proxy solicitation agent, may also solicit proxies by telephone, email, facsimile or Internet. If the Company records votes through the Internet or by telephone, it
will use procedures designed to authenticate Stockholders&#146; identities to allow Stockholders to authorize the voting of their shares in accordance with their instructions and to confirm that their identities have been properly recorded. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company will pay the expenses associated with this Proxy Statement and solicitation, in a manner agreed upon by the Board. The Company has
engaged Computershare Inc. and Broadridge Financial Services, Inc. to assist in the distribution of the proxy materials and tabulation of proxies. The cost of such services with respect to the Company is estimated to be approximately $42,500, plus
reasonable <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">out-of-pocket</FONT></FONT> expenses. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">To vote by mail, sign,
date and promptly return the enclosed proxy card in the accompanying postage <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">pre-paid</FONT> envelope. To vote by Internet or telephone, please use the control number on your proxy card and follow the instructions as
described on your proxy card. If you have any questions regarding the proxy materials, please contact the Company at (888) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">916-1722.</FONT> <B>If the enclosed proxy card is properly executed and received prior to the
Meeting and has not been revoked, the shares represented thereby will be voted in accordance with the instructions marked on the returned proxy card. If no instructions are marked, the proxy card will be voted &#147;FOR&#148; each of the Proposals
described in this Proxy Statement. In either case, shares will be voted in the discretion of the persons named as proxies in connection with any other matter that may properly come before the Meeting or any adjournment(s) or postponement(s)
thereof.</B> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Any person giving a proxy may revoke it at any time before it is exercised (1)&nbsp;by notifying the Secretary of the
Company in writing at the Company&#146;s principal executive offices, (2)&nbsp;by submitting a properly executed, later-dated proxy or (3)&nbsp;by attending the virtual Meeting and voting during the webcast. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">If (i)&nbsp;you are a member of a household in which multiple Stockholders share the same address, (ii)&nbsp;your shares are held in
&#147;street name&#148; and (iii)&nbsp;your broker or bank has received consent to household material, then your broker or bank may send to your household only one copy of this Proxy Statement, unless your broker or bank previously received contrary
instructions from a Stockholder in your household. If you are part of a household that has received only one copy of this Proxy Statement, the Company will deliver promptly a separate copy of this Proxy Statement to you upon written or oral request.
To receive a separate copy of this Proxy Statement, please contact the Company by calling (toll-free) (888) <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">916-1722</FONT> or by mail to the Company&#146;s principal executive offices at Goldman Sachs BDC, Inc., 200
West Street, New York, New York 10282. If your shares are held with certain banks, trust companies, brokers, dealers, investment advisers and other financial </P>

by the closing sales price of the Company&#146;s common stock as reported on the New York Stock Exchange (the &#147;NYSE&#148;) on May&nbsp;11, 2020. </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">5 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>PROPOSAL 1 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ELECTION OF DIRECTORS </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board is divided into three classes with staggered three-year terms. At each annual meeting of Stockholders, the successors to the class
of directors whose term expires at such meeting will be elected to hold office for a term expiring at the annual meeting of Stockholders held in the third year following the year of their election. At the Meeting, you will be asked to elect two
Class&nbsp;III directors to serve until the 2023 annual meeting of stockholders or until his or her successor is duly elected and qualified or until his or her earlier death, resignation, removal or disqualification. In addition, the Board has
adopted policies which provide that (a)&nbsp;no director shall hold office for more than 15 years and (b)&nbsp;a director shall retire as of December 31st of the calendar year in which he or she reaches his or her 74th birthday, unless a waiver of
such requirement has been adopted by a majority of the other directors. These policies may be changed by the directors without a stockholder vote. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Information concerning the nominees and other relevant factors is provided below. Using the enclosed proxy card or voting by the Internet or
by telephone, a Stockholder may vote his or her shares for or against, or abstain from voting with respect to, the election of either nominee. If the enclosed proxy card is properly executed and received prior to the Meeting (and has not been
revoked) but no instructions are marked, the proxies will vote &#147;FOR&#148; the nominees. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Each of Mr.&nbsp;Ross&nbsp;J. Kari and
Ms.&nbsp;Ann&nbsp;B. Lane has consented to his or her nomination and has agreed to continue to serve if elected. If, at the time of the Meeting, for any reason, Mr.&nbsp;Kari or Ms.&nbsp;Lane is not available for election or is not able to serve as
a director, the persons named as proxies intend to exercise their voting power in favor of such person as is nominated by the Board as a substitute. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ON MAY&nbsp;4, 2020, THE BOARD, INCLUDING EACH OF THE INDEPENDENT DIRECTORS, UNANIMOUSLY RECOMMENDED THAT YOU VOTE &#147;FOR&#148; EACH
NOMINEE LISTED ABOVE. </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Information about the Nominees and Directors </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Set forth below are the names of the nominees for Class&nbsp;III directors, as well as each of the continuing directors, and their addresses,
ages, terms of office, principal occupations for at least the past five years and any other directorships they hold in companies which are subject to the reporting requirements of the Exchange Act or are registered as investment companies under the
1940 Act. Directors (including one of the nominees) who (1)&nbsp;are not deemed to be &#147;interested persons,&#148; as defined in the 1940 Act, of the Company, (2)&nbsp;meet the definition of &#147;independent directors&#148; under the corporate
governance standards of the NYSE and (3)&nbsp;meet the independence requirements of Section&nbsp;10A(m)(3) of the Exchange Act are referred to as &#147;Independent Directors.&#148; Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke is deemed to be an &#147;interested person&#148; of
the Company and is referred to as the &#147;Interested Director.&#148; </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Each of Mr.&nbsp;Kari and Ms.&nbsp;Lane has been nominated for
election as a Class&nbsp;III director to serve until the 2023 annual meeting of stockholders. Neither of the nominees are being proposed for election pursuant to any agreement or understanding between such nominee and the Company. </P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Each nominee and director may be contacted by writing to the nominee or director, c/o Goldman Sachs Asset

director&#146;s particular experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills is considered by the Board on an individual basis. Experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills common to all nominees and directors include the ability to
critically review, evaluate and discuss information provided to them and to interact effectively with the other directors and with representatives of GSAM and its affiliates, other service providers, legal counsel and the Company&#146;s independent
registered public accounting firm, the capacity to address financial and legal issues and exercise reasonable business judgment, and a commitment to the representation of the interests of the Company and the Stockholders. The Governance and
Nominating Committee&#146;s charter contains certain other factors that are considered by the Governance and Nominating Committee in identifying and evaluating potential nominees to serve as Independent Directors. Based on each nominee&#146;s
experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills, considered individually and with respect to the experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills of the other directors, the Board has concluded that each nominee should continue to serve as
a director. Below is a brief discussion of the experience, qualifications, attributes and/or skills of each nominee, as well as of the continuing directors, that led the Board to conclude that such individual should serve as a director. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Class&nbsp;III Director Nominees </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Independent
Directors </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Ross J. Kari.</B> Mr.&nbsp;Kari was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in August 2015. Mr.&nbsp;Kari is
retired. He also serves on the Board of Directors of Goldman Sachs Private Middle Market Credit LLC (&#147;PMMC&#148;) and </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">9 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
Goldman Sachs Private Middle Market Credit II LLC (&#147;PMMC II&#148;). Previously, Mr.&nbsp;Kari was Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer of Federal Home Loan Mortgage
Corporation (Freddie Mac), where he worked for four years. Previously, he held senior management positions at SAFECO Corporation, a personal insurance company, Federal Home Loan Bank of San Francisco, and Wells Fargo&nbsp;&amp; Company, where he
began his career and worked for 19 years. Mr.&nbsp;Kari also serves as a Director and a member of the Audit Committee and ALCO Chairman of Summit Bank. Based on the foregoing, Mr.&nbsp;Kari is experienced with financial and investment matters. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Ann B. Lane.</B> Ms.&nbsp;Lane was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in February 2016. Ms.&nbsp;Lane is retired. She also
serves on the Board of Directors of PMMC and PMMC II. Ms.&nbsp;Lane was a Director of Dealertrack Technologies, Inc., an automotive software solutions and services company, from 2007 to 2015. Previously, she worked for five years at JPMorgan
Chase&nbsp;&amp; Co., a financial services company, as a Managing Director and <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Co-Head</FONT> of Syndicated&nbsp;&amp; Leveraged Finance and Head of Loan Syndications Capital Markets. Prior to joining JPMorgan
Chase&nbsp;&amp; Co., Ms.&nbsp;Lane held several senior management positions at Citigroup, Inc., a financial services company, where she worked for 18 years. Based on the foregoing, Ms.&nbsp;Lane is experienced with financial and investment matters.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Continuing Directors not up for <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">re-election</FONT> at the Meeting </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Independent Directors </I></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Jaime
Ardila.</B> Mr.&nbsp;Ardila was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in February 2016 and as Chairman of the Board in January 2018. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila is retired. He also serves as a member and Chairman of the Board of Directors of PMMC and
PMMC II. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila is a member of the Board of Directors of Accenture plc, a management consulting services company, where he serves as Chair of the Finance Committee and a member of the Audit Committee, and a member of the Board of Directors
of Nexa Resources S.A., an oil and gas company. Previously, he was a member of the Board of Directors of Ecopetrol, an integrated oil company, where he served as Chair of the Audit Committee and a member of the Business Committee and the Corporate
Governance and Sustainability Committee, from 2016 to 2019. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila also worked for 29 years at General Motors Company, an automobile manufacturer, where he held several senior management positions, most recently as Executive Vice President
of the company and President of General Motors&#146; South America region. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila joined General Motors in 1984. From 1996 to 1998, Mr.&nbsp;Ardila served as the managing director, Colombian Operations, of N M Rothschild&nbsp;&amp; Sons
Ltd, before rejoining General Motors in 1998. Based on the foregoing, Mr.&nbsp;Ardila is experienced with financial and investment matters. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Susan B. McGee</B>. Ms.&nbsp;McGee was elected to the Board on May&nbsp;1, 2018, with such election effective as of June&nbsp;1, 2018.
Ms.&nbsp;McGee is retired. She also serves on the Board of Directors of PMMC and PMMC II. Ms.&nbsp;McGee worked for 26 years at U.S. Global Investors, Inc., an investment management firm, until June 2018, during which time she held several senior
management positions, including President, General Counsel and Chief Compliance Officer. She has also been involved in the governance of the U.S. Global Investors Funds, serving as Vice President until June 2018. In addition, Ms.&nbsp;McGee serves
on the Board of Governors of the Investment Company Institute and as Chairperson of the Investment Company Institute Small Funds Committee. She also serves as a member of the SEC&#146;s Asset Management Advisory Committee. She is also a member of
the Board of Directors of the San Antonio Sports Foundation, a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">not-for-profit</FONT></FONT> organization, ETTL Engineers and Consultants, and Nobul Corporation, a digital home-buying
marketplace. Based on the foregoing, Ms.&nbsp;McGee is experienced with financial and investment matters. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>Interested Director </I></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Kaysie Uniacke.</B> Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke was elected as one of the Company&#146;s directors in January 2014. Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke is the chair of
the board of Goldman Sachs Asset Management International and MMLC, and serves on the boards of the Goldman Sachs Luxembourg and Dublin family of funds, several GSAM-managed pooled vehicles </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">10 </P>

<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
organized in the Cayman Islands, and PMMC and PMMC II; and is an advisory director to Group Inc. Previously, she was global chief operating officer of GSAM&#146;s portfolio management business
until 2012 and served on the Investment Management Division Client and Business Standards Committee. Prior to this, she was president of Goldman Sachs Trust, the GS mutual fund family, and was head of the Fiduciary Management business within Global
Manager Strategies, responsible for business development and client service globally. Earlier in her career, Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke managed GSAM&#146;s U.S. and Canadian Distribution groups. In that capacity, she was responsible for overseeing all North
American institutional and third-party sales channels, marketing and client service functions, for which client assets exceeded $200&nbsp;billion. Before that, Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke was head of GSAM&#146;s Global Cash Services business, where she was
responsible for overseeing the management of assets exceeding $100&nbsp;billion. Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke worked at Goldman Sachs from 1983 to 2012 where she was named managing director in 1997 and partner in 2002. Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke serves on the board of <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Person-to-Person,</FONT></FONT> a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-profit</FONT> organization that supports the working poor in lower Fairfield County, CT. Based on the foregoing,
Ms.&nbsp;Uniacke is experienced with financial and investment matters. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Compensation of Directors </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">From January&nbsp;1, 2019 to December&nbsp;31, 2019, each Independent Director was compensated with a $100,000 annual fee for his or her
services as director. In addition, the Chairman of the Board earned an additional annual fee of $36,000 and the director designated as the &#147;audit committee financial expert,&#148; as defined in Item 407 of Regulation <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-K,</FONT> earned an additional annual fee of $12,000 for their additional services in these capacities. The Independent Directors are reimbursed for travel and other reasonable expenses incurred in connection with
attending Board and committee meetings. The Company may also pay the incidental costs of a director to attend training or other types of conferences relating to the business development company (&#147;BDC&#148;) industry. In addition, the Company
purchases directors&#146; and officers&#146; liability insurance on behalf of the directors. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">It is the responsibility of the Independent
Directors to review their own compensation and recommend to all of the directors the appropriate level of compensation. This level of compensation may be adjusted from time to time. In conducting their review, the Independent Directors use such
information as they deem relevant, including compensation paid to directors of other BDCs of similar size and the time and effort required of the directors in fulfilling their responsibilities to the Company. </P>

December&nbsp;31, 2019. No compensation is paid by the Company to any Interested Director or executive officer of the Company. </P> <P STYLE="font-size:12pt;margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P STYLE=" margin-top:0pt ; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman; " ALIGN="left">Includes compensation as &#147;audit committee financial expert.&#148; </P></TD></TR></TABLE>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Board Composition and Leadership Structure </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company&#146;s business and affairs are managed under the direction of the Board. The Board consists of five members, four of whom are
Independent Directors. The Board elects the Company&#146;s officers, who serve at the discretion of the Board. The responsibilities of the Board include quarterly valuation of the Company&#146;s assets, corporate governance activities, oversight of
the Company&#146;s financing arrangements and oversight of its investment activities. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board&#146;s role in the management of the
Company is one of oversight. Oversight of the Company&#146;s investment activities extends to oversight of the risk management processes employed by GSAM as part of its
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">day-to-day</FONT></FONT> management of the Company&#146;s investment activities. The Board reviews risk management processes at both regular and special Board meetings throughout the
year, consulting with appropriate representatives of GSAM as necessary and periodically requesting the production of risk management reports or presentations. The goal of the Board&#146;s risk oversight function is to ensure that the risks
associated with the Company&#146;s investment activities are accurately identified, thoroughly investigated and responsibly addressed. Stockholders should note, however, that the Board&#146;s oversight function cannot eliminate all risks or ensure
that particular events do not adversely affect the value of the Company&#146;s investments. The Board also has primary responsibility for the valuation of the Company&#146;s assets. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board has established an Audit Committee, Governance and Nominating Committee, Compensation Committee, Compliance Committee and Contract
Review Committee. The scope of each committee&#146;s responsibilities is discussed in greater detail below. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Jaime Ardila, an Independent
Director, serves as Chairman of the Board. The Board believes that it is in the best interests of the Stockholders for Mr.&nbsp;Ardila to lead the Board because of his familiarity with the Company&#146;s portfolio companies, his broad corporate
background and experience with financial and investment matters and his significant senior management experience, as described above. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila generally acts as a liaison between management, officers and attorneys between meetings of the
Board and presides over all executive sessions of the Independent Directors without management. The Board believes that its leadership structure is appropriate because the structure allocates areas of responsibility among the individual directors
and the committees in a manner that enhances effective oversight. The Board also believes that its size creates an efficient corporate governance structure that provides opportunity for direct communication and interaction between management and the
Board. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Board had six formal meetings in 2019. Each director attended at least 75% of the meetings of the Board and of the respective
committees on which he or she served during the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2019. To promote effectiveness of the Board, under normal circumstances directors are strongly encouraged to attend regularly scheduled Board meetings in person.
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">None of the Company&#146;s directors attended the 2019 Annual Meeting of Stockholders. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Committees of the Board </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Audit Committee
</I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The current members of the Audit Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of whom is
an Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila simultaneously serves on the audit committees of more than three public companies, and the Board has determined that his simultaneous service on the audit committees of other public companies does not impair
his ability to effectively serve on the Audit Committee. Mr.&nbsp;Kari serves as Chairman of the Audit Committee. The Board and the Audit Committee have determined that Mr.&nbsp;Kari is an &#147;audit committee financial expert,&#148; as defined in
Item 407 of Regulation <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-K.</FONT> </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">12 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee is responsible for overseeing matters relating to the appointment and
activities of the Company&#146;s auditors, audit plans and procedures, various accounting and financial reporting issues and changes in accounting policies, and reviewing the results and scope of the audit and other services provided by the
independent public accountants. The Audit Committee is also responsible for aiding the Board in fair value pricing debt and equity securities that are not publicly traded or for which current market values are not readily available. The Audit
Committee&#146;s charter is available on the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee
held six formal meetings in 2019. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Governance and Nominating Committee </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The current members of the Governance and Nominating Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of
whom is an Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila serves as the Chairman of the Governance and Nominating Committee. The Governance and Nominating Committee is responsible for identifying, researching and nominating Independent Directors for election
by the Stockholders, selecting nominees to fill vacancies on the Board or a committee of the Board, developing and recommending to the Board a set of corporate governance principles and overseeing the evaluation of the Board and management. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">All candidates nominated for an Independent Director position must meet applicable independence requirements and have the capacity to address
financial and legal issues and exercise reasonable business judgment. The Governance and Nominating Committee considers a variety of criteria in evaluating candidates (including candidates nominated by a Stockholder), including (1)&nbsp;experience
in business, financial or investment matters or in other fields of endeavor; (2)&nbsp;financial literacy and/or whether he or she is an &#147;audit committee financial expert,&#148; as defined in Item 407 of Regulation
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">S-K;</FONT> (3)&nbsp;reputation; (4) ability to attend scheduled Board and committee meetings; (5)&nbsp;general availability to attend to Board business on short notice; (6)&nbsp;actual or potential business, family
or other conflicts bearing on either the candidate&#146;s independence or the business of the Company; (7)&nbsp;length of potential service; (8)&nbsp;commitment to the representation of the interests of the Company and the Stockholders;
(9)&nbsp;commitment to maintaining and improving his or her skills and education; (10)&nbsp;experience in corporate governance and best business practices; and (11)&nbsp;the diversity that he or she would bring to the Board&#146;s composition. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Governance and Nominating Committee considers nominees properly recommended by a Stockholder. The Company&#146;s bylaws provide that for
any nomination to be properly brought by a Stockholder for a meeting, such Stockholder must comply with advance notice requirements and provide the Company with certain information. Generally, to be timely, a Stockholder&#146;s notice must be
received at the Company&#146;s principal executive offices not less than 90 days nor more than 120 days prior to the first anniversary date of the immediately preceding annual meeting of Stockholders. The Company&#146;s bylaws further provide that
nominations of persons for election to the Board at a special meeting may be made only by or at the direction of the Board and, provided that the Board has determined that directors will be elected at the meeting, by a Stockholder who is entitled to
vote at the meeting and who has complied with the advance notice provisions of the bylaws. The Governance and Nominating Committee&#146;s charter is available on the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Governance and Nominating Committee held three formal meetings in 2019. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Compensation Committee </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
current members of the Compensation Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of whom is an Independent Director. The Compensation Committee is responsible for determining, or recommending to the Board for
determination, the compensation, if any, of the Company&#146;s chief executive officer and all other executive officers. The Compensation Committee also assists the Board with matters related </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">13 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
to compensation generally, except with respect to compensation of the directors. As discussed in &#147;Compensation of Directors,&#148; below, it is the responsibility of the Independent
Directors to review their own compensation and recommend to all of the directors the appropriate level of compensation. As none of the Company&#146;s executive officers currently is compensated by the Company, the Compensation Committee does not
produce and/or review a report on executive compensation practices. The Compensation Committee&#146;s charter is available on the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Compensation Committee did not hold any formal meetings in 2019. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Compliance Committee </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The current
members of the Compliance Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of whom is an Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila serves as Chairman of the Compliance Committee. The Compliance Committee is
responsible for overseeing the Company&#146;s compliance processes, and insofar as they relate to services provided to us, the compliance processes of the investment adviser, underwriters (if any), administrator and transfer agent, except that
compliance processes relating to the accounting and financial reporting processes and certain related matters are overseen by the Audit Committee. In addition, the Compliance Committee provides assistance to the full Board with respect to compliance
matters. The Compliance Committee&#146;s charter is available on the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Compliance Committee held five formal meetings in 2019. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Contract Review Committee </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The
current members of the Contract Review Committee are Mr.&nbsp;Ardila, Mr.&nbsp;Kari, Ms.&nbsp;Lane and Ms.&nbsp;McGee, each of whom is an Independent Director. Mr.&nbsp;Ardila serves as Chairman of the Contract Review Committee. The Contract Review
Committee is responsible for overseeing the processes of the Board for reviewing and monitoring performance under the Company&#146;s investment management, placement agent (if any), principal underwriting (if any) and certain other agreements with
GSAM and its affiliates. The Contract Review Committee also provides appropriate assistance to the Board in connection with the Board&#146;s approval, oversight and review of the Company&#146;s other service providers, including the Company&#146;s
custodian/accounting agent, transfer agent, printing firms, and professional firms (other than the Company&#146;s independent auditor, which is the responsibility of the Audit Committee). The Contract Review Committee&#146;s charter is available on
the Company&#146;s website (<I><U>https://www.goldmansachsbdc.com</U></I>). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Contract Review Committee had two formal meetings in
2019. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Information about Executive Officers who are not Directors </B></P>

<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Brendan McGovern</B>. Mr.&nbsp;McGovern was appointed as the Company&#146;s chief executive officer and president in March 2013.
Mr.&nbsp;McGovern heads GSAM&#146;s Private Credit Group, is the chief executive officer and president of PMMC, PMMC II and MMLC and also serves as <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-head</FONT> and senior portfolio manager of the GSAM Credit
Alternatives portfolio management team. He is also the Chair and a voting member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;McGovern
joined the firm in 2006. Prior to joining the firm, Mr.&nbsp;McGovern served as a managing director in<B> </B>the Global Investment Group at Amaranth Advisors, where he <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-headed</FONT> the fund&#146;s private
placement efforts for both debt and equity linked products in the United States. He is also on the board of directors for the Oxalosis and Hyperoxaluria Foundation. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Jon Yoder</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Yoder was appointed as the Company&#146;s chief operating officer in March 2013. Mr.&nbsp;Yoder is the chief
operating officer of PMMC, PMMC II and MMLC and a member of GSAM&#146;s Private Credit Group with a focus on sourcing, structuring and executing privately negotiated debt financings. He is also a voting member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s
Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;Yoder joined the firm in 2005. Prior to joining the firm, he was a member of the mergers and acquisitions and private equity
groups at Paul, Weiss, Rifkind, Wharton&nbsp;&amp; Garrison, LLP. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Jonathan Lamm</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Lamm was appointed as the Company&#146;s
chief financial officer and treasurer in March 2013. Mr.&nbsp;Lamm is also the chief financial officer and treasurer of PMMC, PMMC II and MMLC and chief operating officer of the GSAM Credit Alternatives portfolio management team, responsible for the
operations of the business, including business financials, infrastructure support, and IT project management, as well as the continuous improvement of the control environment. Mr.&nbsp;Lamm is secretary and a
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-voting</FONT> member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. He joined the firm in 2002. Prior to joining
the firm, Mr.&nbsp;Lamm worked in the securities audit practice at Deloitte&nbsp;&amp; Touche LLP. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Julien Yoo</B>. Ms.&nbsp;Yoo is the
chief compliance officer of the Company and has served in such capacity since June 2019. Ms.&nbsp;Yoo is also the chief compliance officer of PMMC, PMMC II, MMLC, Goldman Sachs Trust, Goldman Sachs Variable Insurance Trust, Goldman Sachs Trust II,
Goldman Sachs MLP Income Opportunities Fund, Goldman Sachs MLP and Energy Renaissance Fund, Goldman Sachs ETF Trust and Goldman Sachs Real Estate Diversified Income Fund. Ms.&nbsp;Yoo joined Goldman Sachs in 2013.&nbsp;Prior to joining Goldman
Sachs, Ms.&nbsp;Yoo was a Vice President in the legal department of Morgan Stanley Investment Management. Prior to joining Morgan Stanley, she was an associate at Shearman&nbsp;&amp; Sterling, LLP and at Swidler Berlin Shereff Friedman, LLP. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>David Yu</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Yu was appointed as an executive vice president and Head of Research of the Company in March 2013. Mr.&nbsp;Yu is
executive vice president and Head of Research of PMMC, PMMC II and MMLC and a member of the GSAM Private Credit Group with a focus on sourcing, structuring and executing privately negotiated debt financings and serves as its Head of Research.
Mr.&nbsp;Yu is a voting member of the Private Credit Group&#146;s Investment Committee, which is responsible for evaluating and approving all of the Company&#146;s investments. Mr.&nbsp;Yu joined the firm in 2006. Prior to joining the firm,
Mr.&nbsp;Yu was an associate in the Global Investments Group at Amaranth Advisors, where he similarly worked with public and private issuers to structure and execute debt and equity financings. Prior to joining Amaranth, he worked in the Leveraged
Finance and Sponsor Coverage Group at CIBC World Markets. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Michael Mastropaolo</B>. Mr.&nbsp;Mastropaolo was appointed as an executive
vice president of the Company in February 2019. Mr.&nbsp;Mastropaolo is executive vice president of PMMC. PMMC II and MMLC and a member of the GSAM Credit Alternatives team with a focus on sourcing, structuring and executing privately negotiated
debt </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">15 </P>

Mr.&nbsp;Pessah is Principal Accounting Officer of PMMC, PMMC II and MMLC. Mr.&nbsp;Pessah is a Vice President in the BDC Fund Controllers team of Goldman Sachs Asset Management, L.P., the Company&#146;s investment adviser. Mr.&nbsp;Pessah is
responsible for fund accounting and financial reporting oversight as well as the continuous improvement of the control environment for the Company. Prior to joining Goldman Sachs in September 2010, he worked in the audit practice at Ernst&nbsp;&amp;
Young LLP. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Certain Relationships and Related Party Transactions </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Investment Management Agreement </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company is party to an investment management agreement, pursuant to which the Company pays GSAM, a wholly owned subsidiary of Group Inc., a
fee for investment management services consisting of a management fee based on the Company&#146;s gross assets (excluding cash and cash equivalents but including assets purchased with borrowed amounts) and an incentive fee based on the performance
of the Company&#146;s investments. Certain of the Company&#146;s officers are also officers and employees of GSAM. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2019, the management fee was calculated at an annual rate of 1.00% (0.25% per quarter) of the average value of the Company&#146;s gross assets at the end of each of the two most recently completed calendar quarters. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">For the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2019, the Company paid GSAM a total of $21.46&nbsp;million in fees (excluding fees that are accrued but
not paid) pursuant to the investment management agreement, which consisted of $14.48&nbsp;million in management fees and $6.98&nbsp;million in incentive fees. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>License Agreement </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company is
party to a license agreement with an affiliate of Goldman Sachs pursuant to which the Company has been granted a <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">non-exclusive,</FONT> royalty-free license to use the &#147;Goldman Sachs&#148; name. Under this
agreement, the Company does not have a right to use the Goldman Sachs name if GSAM or another affiliate of Goldman Sachs is not the Company&#146;s investment adviser or if the Company&#146;s continued use of such license results in a violation of
applicable law, results in a regulatory burden or has adverse regulatory consequences. Other than with respect to this limited license, the Company has no legal right to the &#147;Goldman Sachs&#148; name. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Co-Investment</FONT> Opportunities </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Company has in the past <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-invested,</FONT> and in the future may
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-invest,</FONT> on a concurrent basis with other funds managed by GSAM and its affiliates, but not if such <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-investment</FONT> is impermissible under existing
</P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">16 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
regulatory guidance, applicable regulations or GSAM&#146;s allocation procedures. Certain types of negotiated <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-investments</FONT> may be made only if the
Company receives an order from the SEC permitting the Company to do so. On January&nbsp;4, 2017, the SEC granted the Company, PMMC and MMLC, as well as certain other funds managed by GSAM in the future, the exemptive relief to make negotiated <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">co-investments,</FONT> subject to certain terms and conditions in the exemptive relief. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>Related Party Transaction Review
Policy </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee will review any potential related party transactions brought to its attention, and, during these reviews,
will consider any conflicts of interest brought to its attention pursuant to the Company&#146;s Code of Ethics. Each of the Company&#146;s directors and executive officers is instructed and periodically reminded to inform GSAM Compliance of any
potential related party transactions. In addition, each such director and executive officer completes a questionnaire on an annual basis designed to elicit information about any potential related party transactions. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">17 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>PROPOSAL 2 </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>RATIFICATION OF SELECTION OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM </B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">At a meeting of the Board held on December&nbsp;3, 2019, the Audit Committee selected and recommended, and the Board, including a majority of
the Independent Directors approved, the selection of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP to act as the independent registered public accounting firm for the Company for the fiscal year ending December&nbsp;31, 2020. This selection is presented for
ratification by the Stockholders. If the Stockholders fail to ratify the selection of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP to serve as the independent registered public accounting firm for the year ending December&nbsp;31, 2020, the Audit Committee and the
Board will reconsider the continued retention of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Representatives of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP are expected
to be available telephonically during the Meeting and will be available to respond to appropriate questions from Stockholders if necessary. Representatives of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP will be given the opportunity to make statements at the
Meeting, if they so desire. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Audit Fees </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The aggregate audit fees billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018 were $845,000 and $808,500,
respectively. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Fees included in the audit fees category are those associated with the annual audits of financial statements, review of the
financial statements included in the Company&#146;s Quarterly Reports on <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Form&nbsp;10-Q&nbsp;and</FONT> services that are normally provided in connection with statutory and regulatory filings. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Audit-Related Fees </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The aggregate
audit-related fees billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018 were $33,500 and $0, respectively. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Audit-related fees are for any services rendered to the Company that are reasonably related to the performance of the audits or reviews of the
Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements (but not reported as audit fees above). These services include attestation services that are not required by statute or regulation and consultations concerning financial accounting and reporting
standards. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The aggregate audit-related fees billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP to GSAM, and any entity controlling, controlled by, or
under common control with, GSAM, that provides ongoing services to the Company, for engagements directly related to the Company&#146;s operations and financial reporting, for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018 were $1,200,400 and
$1,133,433, respectively. These amounts represent fees PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP billed to GSAM for services related to the SSAE 18 report. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>Tax
Fees </I></B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The aggregate fees billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for services rendered to the Company for tax compliance, tax advice
and tax planning for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018 were $0 and $58,750, respectively. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Fees included in the tax fees
category comprise all services performed by professional staff in the independent registered public accountant&#146;s tax division except those services related to the audits. This category comprises fees for tax compliance services provided in
connection with the preparation and review of the Company&#146;s tax returns. </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">18 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">No tax fees were billed by the Company&#146;s independent registered public accountant to GSAM,
and any entity controlling, controlled by, or under common control with, GSAM, that provides ongoing services to the Company, for engagements directly related to the Company&#146;s operations and financial reporting, for the years ended
December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I>All Other Fees </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">No fees were billed by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP for products and services provided to the Company, other than the services reported in
&#147;Audit Fees&#148; and &#147;Tax Fees&#148; above, for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Other than services reported
under &#147;Audit-Related Fees,&#148; no other fees were billed by the Company&#146;s independent registered public accountant to GSAM, and any entity controlling, controlled by, or under common control with, GSAM, that provides ongoing services to
the Company, for engagements directly related to the Company&#146;s operations and financial reporting, for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Aggregate&nbsp;Non-Audit&nbsp;Fees</FONT> </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">No&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;fees</FONT> were billed to the Company&#146;s investment adviser and service affiliates
by PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">for&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT> for the years ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 and 2018. This includes <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">any&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT>
required to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">be&nbsp;pre-approved&nbsp;or&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT></FONT> that did not <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">require&nbsp;pre-approval&nbsp;since</FONT> they did
not directly relate to the Company&#146;s operations or financial reporting. </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Pre-Approval</FONT> of Audit and <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Non-Audit</FONT> Services Provided to the Company </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">and&nbsp;Non-Audit&nbsp;Services&nbsp;Pre-Approval&nbsp;Policy</FONT></FONT> (the &#147;Policy&#148;) adopted by the Audit Committee sets forth the procedures and the conditions pursuant to which services performed by an
independent auditor for the Company may <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">be&nbsp;pre-approved.&nbsp;Services</FONT> may <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">be&nbsp;pre-approved&nbsp;specifically</FONT> by the Audit Committee as a whole or, in certain
circumstances, by the Audit Committee Chairman or the person designated as the audit committee financial expert. In addition, subject to specified cost limitations, certain services may
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">be&nbsp;pre-approved&nbsp;under</FONT> the provisions of the Policy. The Policy provides that the Audit Committee will consider whether the services provided by an independent auditor are consistent with the
SEC&#146;s rules on auditor independence. The Policy provides for periodic review <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">and&nbsp;pre-approval&nbsp;by</FONT> the Audit Committee of the services that may be provided by the independent auditor. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I>De Minimis Waiver</I>. <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">The&nbsp;pre-approval&nbsp;requirements</FONT> of the Policy may be waived with
respect to the provision <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT> that are permissible for an independent auditor to perform, provided (1)&nbsp;the aggregate amount of all such services provided constitutes no more
than five percent of the total amount of revenues subject <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">to&nbsp;pre-approval&nbsp;that</FONT> was paid to the independent auditors during the fiscal year in which the services are provided; (2)&nbsp;such services
were not recognized by the Company at the time of the engagement to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">be&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services;</FONT> and (3)&nbsp;such services are promptly brought to the attention of the Audit Committee and approved prior
to the completion of the audit by the Audit Committee or by one or more members of the Audit Committee to whom authority to grant such approvals has been delegated by the Audit Committee, pursuant to
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">the&nbsp;pre-approval&nbsp;provisions</FONT> of the Policy. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Pre-Approval</FONT></I><I></I><I>&nbsp;of</I><I></I><I><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">&nbsp;
Non-Audit</FONT></I><I></I><I>&nbsp;Services Provided to GSAM.</I>&nbsp;The Policy provides that, in addition to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">requiring&nbsp;pre-approval&nbsp;of</FONT> audit
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">and&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT> provided to the Company, the Audit Committee
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap"><FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">will&nbsp;pre-approve&nbsp;those&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT></FONT> provided to the Company&#146;s investment adviser (and entities controlling, controlled by or under common
control with the investment adviser that provide ongoing services to the Company) where the engagement relates directly to the operations or financial reporting of the Company. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit Committee has considered these fees and the nature of the services rendered, and has concluded that they are compatible with
maintaining the independence of PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP. The Audit </P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">19 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">
Committee did not approve any of the audit-related, tax, or <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">other&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;fees</FONT> described above pursuant to the &#147;<I>de
minimis</I>&nbsp;exceptions&#148; set forth in <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Rule&nbsp;2-01(c)(7)(i)(C)&nbsp;and</FONT> <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Rule&nbsp;2-01(c)(7)(ii)&nbsp;of</FONT>
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Regulation&nbsp;S-X.&nbsp;Except</FONT> as described above, PricewaterhouseCoopers LLP did not provide any audit-related services, tax services or
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">other&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT> to GSAM or any entity controlling, controlled by or under common control with GSAM that provides ongoing services to the Company that the Audit Committee was required to
approve pursuant to <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Rule&nbsp;2-01(c)(7)(ii)&nbsp;of</FONT> <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">Regulation&nbsp;S-X.&nbsp;The</FONT> Audit Committee considered whether the provision
<FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">of&nbsp;non-audit&nbsp;services</FONT> rendered to GSAM and any entity controlling, controlled by, or under common control with GSAM that provides ongoing services to the Company that were <FONT
STYLE="white-space:nowrap">not&nbsp;pre-approved&nbsp;by</FONT> the Audit Committee because the engagement did not relate directly to the operations and financial reporting of the Company is compatible with maintaining PricewaterhouseCoopers
LLP&#146;s independence.<B></B> </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B>ON MAY&nbsp;4, 2020, THE BOARD, INCLUDING EACH OF THE INDEPENDENT DIRECTORS, UNANIMOUSLY RECOMMENDED
THAT YOU VOTE &#147;FOR&#148; THE RATIFICATION OF PRICEWATERHOUSECOOPERS LLP AS INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM TO THE COMPANY FOR THE FISCAL YEAR ENDING DECEMBER&nbsp;31, 2020. </B></P>
 <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center">20 </P>


<p style="margin-top:1em; margin-bottom:0em; page-break-before:always">
<HR SIZE="3" style="COLOR:#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman" ALIGN="center"><B><I>Audit Committee Report <SUP STYLE="font-size:85%; vertical-align:top">(1)</SUP> </I></B></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The following is the report of the Audit Committee of Goldman Sachs BDC, Inc. (the &#147;Company&#148;) with respect to the Company&#146;s
audited financial statements for the fiscal year ended December&nbsp;31, 2019 (the &#147;Audited Financial Statements&#148;). </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The Audit
Committee has: (a)&nbsp;reviewed and discussed the Audited Financial Statements with the management of the Company; (b)&nbsp;discussed with the independent auditor the matters required to be discussed by Auditing Standard 1301 (Communications with
Audit Committees), as adopted by the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (&#147;PCAOB&#148;); and (c)&nbsp;received the written disclosures and the letter from the independent auditor required by applicable requirements of the PCAOB Ethics and
Independence Rule 3526 regarding the independent auditor&#146;s communications with the Audit Committee concerning independence, and has discussed with the independent auditor the auditor&#146;s independence. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">The members of the Audit Committee are not, and do not represent themselves to be, professionally engaged in the practice of auditing or
accounting and are not employed by the Company for accounting, financial management or internal control purposes. Moreover, the Audit Committee relies on and makes no independent verification of the facts presented to it or representations made by
management or the Company&#146;s independent auditor. Accordingly, the Audit Committee&#146;s oversight does not provide an independent basis to determine that management has maintained appropriate accounting and/or financial reporting principles
and policies, or internal controls and procedures designed to assure compliance with accounting standards and applicable laws and regulations. Furthermore, the Audit Committee&#146;s considerations and discussions referred to above do not provide
assurance that the audit of the Company&#146;s financial statements has been carried out in accordance with the standards of the PCAOB or that the financial statements are presented in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Based on its consideration of the Audited Financial Statements and the discussions referred to above with management and the Company&#146;s
independent auditor, and subject to the limitations on the responsibilities and role of the Audit Committee set forth in the charter and those discussed above, the Audit Committee recommended to the Board of Directors that the Audited Financial
Statements be accepted by the Board of Directors and included in the Company&#146;s Annual Report on Form <FONT STYLE="white-space:nowrap">10-K</FONT> for the last fiscal year for filing with the SEC. </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:12pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">February&nbsp;26, 2020 </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; text-indent:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman"><B>The
Audit Committee </B></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ross J. Kari, Chairman </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Jaime Ardila </P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Ann B. Lane </P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:0pt; margin-bottom:0pt; margin-left:4%; font-size:10pt; font-family:Times New Roman">Susan B. McGee </P> <p STYLE="margin-top:0pt;margin-bottom:0pt ; font-size:8pt">&nbsp;</P>
